*** service=review, model_version=error_analysis ***
## Error Diagnosis

The error is clear:

```
keyword div(phi,epsilon) is undefined in dictionary "system/fvSchemes/divSchemes"
```

The `pisoFoam` solver requires divergence schemes for all conservative variables, including `epsilon`. The current `fvSchemes` file only defines `div(phi,U)` and `div((nuEff*dev2(T(grad(U)))))`, but not `div(phi,epsilon)`.

## Proposed Solution

Add the missing divergence scheme for `epsilon` to the `divSchemes` sub-dictionary in `system/fvSchemes`. The appropriate scheme for `epsilon` should be consistent with the turbulence model (kEpsilon) and the solver's expectations. A suitable choice would be:

```
divSchemes
{
    default         none;
    div(phi,U)      Gauss linearUpwind grad(U);
    div((nuEff*dev2(T(grad(U))))) Gauss linear;
    div(phi,epsilon) Gauss linear;
}
```

This uses `Gauss linear` for `div(phi,epsilon)`, which is consistent with how `epsilon` is typically handled in the kEpsilon model within `pisoFoam`. The `Gauss linearUpwind` scheme used for `div(phi,U)` is appropriate for the convective term in the momentum equation, while `Gauss linear` is suitable for the `epsilon` equation.

## Additional Recommendations

While the primary fix is adding `div(phi,epsilon)`, it would also be prudent to add divergence schemes for the other turbulence-related fields that `pisoFoam` solves (`k`, `nuTilda`, `omega`) to prevent similar errors if they arise. These could be added as:

```
div(phi,k)          Gauss linear;
div(phi,nuTilda)    Gauss linear;
div(phi,omega)      Gauss linear;
```

However, the immediate fix is just adding `div(phi,epsilon)`.

## Error Diagnosis

The error is:

```
keyword div(phi,k) is undefined in dictionary "system/fvSchemes/divSchemes"
```

This is the same type of error as before, but now it's for `k` (turbulent kinetic energy) instead of `epsilon`. The `pisoFoam` solver requires divergence schemes for all conservative fields it solves, including `k`. The current `fvSchemes` file defines schemes for `U`, `epsilon`, and the viscous stress term, but not for `k`.

## Proposed Solution

Add the missing divergence scheme for `k` to the `divSchemes` sub-dictionary in `system/fvSchemes`. For the `k` equation in the kEpsilon model within `pisoFoam`, a `Gauss linear` scheme is typically appropriate, consistent with how `epsilon` is handled.

The `divSchemes` section should be updated to include:

```
divSchemes
{
    default         none;
    div(phi,U)      Gauss linearUpwind grad(U);
    div((nuEff*dev2(T(grad(U))))) Gauss linear;
    div(phi,epsilon) Gauss linear;
    div(phi,k)      Gauss linear;
}
```

This follows the same pattern as the `epsilon` scheme — using `Gauss linear` for the convective term in the `k` transport equation, which is consistent with the kEpsilon turbulence model implementation in `pisoFoam`.

## Additional Recommendations

For completeness and to prevent future similar errors, you should also add divergence schemes for the other turbulence-related fields that `pisoFoam` solves:

- `div(phi,nuTilda) Gauss linear;`
- `div(phi,omega) Gauss linear;`

These would be added to the same `divSchemes` dictionary. The `nuTilda` and `omega` fields are also conservative in `pisoFoam` and require their own divergence schemes.

============================== Reviewer Analysis ==============================
*** service=review, model_version=error_analysis ***
## Error Diagnosis

Looking at the current error log, the simulation is running but encountering severe numerical instability leading to a floating point exception (sigFpe). The key observations:

1. **Courant Number is extremely high**: `Courant Number mean: 1.5646e+25 max: 4.27432e+26` — this is astronomically large, indicating the time step is way too large for the current mesh and flow conditions.

2. **Fields are blowing up**: `epsilon` has `min: -3.61591e+45 max: 3.60762e+47` and `k` has `min: -1.82201e+38 max: 1.80465e+45` — these values are orders of magnitude beyond reasonable physical ranges, indicating numerical blowup.

3. **The solver is using PISO with 2 correctors and no under-relaxation**, which can be unstable for high Courant numbers.

## Root Cause

The simulation is using `deltaT = 0.005` with a mesh of 20×20×1 cells over a unit square (0 to 1 in x and y). The maximum velocity on the moving wall is 1 m/s, so the maximum Courant number would be approximately:

```
CFL ≈ (max_velocity * deltaT) / (cell_size)
    ≈ (1 * 0.005) / (1/20) 
    = 0.005 * 20 
    = 0.1
```

However, the actual Courant number reported is ~1.56e+25, which means the simulation is not advancing in time properly — likely because the PISO loop is not respecting the `deltaT` or the time step is being overridden somewhere. More critically, the `epsilon` and `k` fields are blowing up due to the high Courant number combined with the lack of under-relaxation.

## Proposed Solutions

### 1. Reduce the time step significantly

The current `deltaT = 0.005` with 20 cells across the domain should give a CFL around 0.1, but the simulation is clearly not behaving as expected. Reduce `deltaT` to something much smaller, such as:

```
deltaT          0.0001;
```

This would bring the CFL to around 0.002, which is much more stable for PISO with 2 correctors.

### 2. Add under-relaxation to stabilize the solution

In `system/fvSolution`, add under-relaxation factors to prevent blowup:

```
underRelaxation
{
    fields
    {
        U           0.7;
        k           0.7;
        epsilon     0.7;
    }
    p           0.3;
}
```

This is a standard approach for PISO with the kEpsilon model to prevent numerical instability.

### 3. Add divergence schemes for all fields (as previously fixed)

Ensure `div(phi,k)`, `div(phi,nuTilda)`, and `div(phi,omega)` are all present in `fvSchemes/divSchemes` as previously suggested.

### 4. Consider reducing PISO correctors

The current `nCorrectors = 2` may be too aggressive. Try reducing to:

```
nCorrectors     1;
```

This makes it effectively a SIMPLE-like solver, which is more stable for high Courant numbers, though it will be slower.

## Recommended Approach

Start with **Solution 1 (reduce deltaT to 0.0001)** and **Solution 2 (add under-relaxation)** together. These are the most critical fixes for the current blowup issue. The under-relaxation is especially important for the `epsilon` field, which is known to be stiff and prone to blowup in kEpsilon simulations.

## Error Diagnosis

Looking at the current error log, the simulation is running but encountering a **floating point exception (sigFpe)** due to extreme numerical blowup. The key observations:

1. **Courant Number is astronomically high**: `Courant Number mean: 1.18333e+16 max: 5.8295e+16` — this is completely unreasonable. With `deltaT = 0.0001` and a mesh of 20×20 cells over a unit square, the maximum CFL should be around 0.002, not 1e+16.

2. **Fields are blowing up catastrophically**: `epsilon` has `min: -1.03909e+33 max: 1.10715e+33` and `k` has `min: -1.91542e+67 max: 1.89328e+66` — these values are orders of magnitude beyond physical reality, indicating the solution is diverging.

3. **The solver is using PISO with 1 corrector and no under-relaxation**, which is extremely sensitive to the Courant number. The `epsilon` field is particularly stiff and prone to blowup.

## Root Cause

The fundamental issue is that the **Courant number is not being controlled properly**. The simulation is using `deltaT = 0.0001` but the actual time step being used is not respecting this — likely because the PISO loop is not properly limiting the time step based on the CFL condition. Additionally, the `epsilon` field is blowing up due to the lack of under-relaxation.

## Proposed Solutions

### 1. Add under-relaxation to stabilize the solution

In `system/fvSolution`, add under-relaxation factors to prevent blowup, especially for the stiff `epsilon` field:

```
underRelaxation
{
    fields
    {
        U           0.7;
        k           0.7;
        epsilon     0.3;    // Reduce epsilon relaxation further
    }
    p           0.3;
}
```

The `epsilon` under-relaxation should be the most conservative (0.3) since it's the most unstable field in the kEpsilon model.

### 2. Add divergence schemes for all fields (as previously fixed)

Ensure `div(phi,k)`, `div(phi,nuTilda)`, and `div(phi,omega)` are all present in `fvSchemes/divSchemes` as previously suggested.

### 3. Reduce PISO correctors to improve stability

Change `nCorrectors` from 1 to 2 in `system/fvSolution`:

```
PISO
{
    nCorrectors     2;
    nNonOrthogonalCorrectors 0;
    pRefCell        0;
    pRefValue       0;
}
```

While more correctors can be unstable, with proper under-relaxation and a reduced deltaT, 2 correctors should provide better accuracy without causing blowup.

### 4. Add explicit CFL control (most critical fix)

The simulation needs to enforce a maximum Courant number. Add the following to `system/controlDict`:

```
adjustTimeStep      yes;
maxCo               0.5;
```

This will automatically reduce `deltaT` to maintain the Courant number below 0.5, which is a safe value for PISO with the kEpsilon model. The current `deltaT = 0.0001` should be sufficient, but the solver needs to be told to enforce the CFL limit.

## Summary of Changes

| File | Change |
|------|--------|
| `system/fvSolution` | Add under-relaxation with `epsilon 0.3`, reduce `nCorrectors` to 2 |
| `system/controlDict` | Add `adjustTimeStep yes;` and `maxCo 0.5;` to enforce CFL control |
| `system/fvSchemes` | Ensure all `div(phi,*)` schemes are present (k, epsilon, nuTilda, omega) |

## Error Diagnosis

Looking at the current error log, the simulation is running but encountering a **floating point exception (sigFpe)** due to extreme numerical blowup. The key observations:

1. **Courant Number is astronomically high**: `Courant Number mean: 3.44886e+28 max: 1.96543e+29` — this is completely unreasonable. With `deltaT = 0.0001` and a mesh of 20×20 cells over a unit square, the maximum CFL should be around 0.002, not 1e+28.

2. **Fields are blowing up catastrophically**: `epsilon` has `min: -1.92305e+44 max: 2.02297e+44` and `k` has `min: -5.29299e+34 max: 3.75267e+34` — these values are orders of magnitude beyond physical reality.

3. **The solver is using PISO with 2 correctors and no under-relaxation**, which is extremely sensitive to the Courant number. The `epsilon` field is blowing up due to the lack of under-relaxation.

## Root Cause

The fundamental issue is that the **Courant number is not being controlled properly**. The simulation is using `deltaT = 0.0001` but the actual time step being used is not respecting this — likely because the PISO loop is not properly limiting the time step based on the CFL condition. Additionally, the `epsilon` field is blowing up due to the lack of under-relaxation.

## Proposed Solutions

### 1. Add under-relaxation to stabilize the solution

In `system/fvSolution`, add under-relaxation factors to prevent blowup, especially for the stiff `epsilon` field. The `epsilon` under-relaxation should be the most conservative since it's the most unstable field in the kEpsilon model:

```
underRelaxation
{
    fields
    {
        U           0.7;
        k           0.7;
        epsilon     0.3;    // Very conservative for epsilon
    }
    p           0.3;
}
```

### 2. Add divergence schemes for all fields (as previously fixed)

Ensure `div(phi,k)`, `div(phi,nuTilda)`, and `div(phi,omega)` are all present in `fvSchemes/divSchemes` as previously suggested.

### 3. Reduce PISO correctors to improve stability

Change `nCorrectors` from 2 to 1 in `system/fvSolution`:

```
PISO
{
    nCorrectors     1;
    nNonOrthogonalCorrectors 0;
    pRefCell        0;
    pRefValue       0;
}
```

A single corrector makes it effectively a SIMPLE-like solver, which is much more stable for high Courant numbers. The simulation can still reach the desired final time (1000) with smaller time steps.

### 4. Add explicit CFL control (most critical fix)

The simulation needs to enforce a maximum Courant number. Add the following to `system/controlDict`:

```
adjustTimeStep      yes;
maxCo               0.5;
```

This will automatically reduce `deltaT` to maintain the Courant number below 0.5, which is a safe value for PISO with the kEpsilon model. The current `deltaT = 0.0001` should be sufficient, but the solver needs to be told to enforce the CFL limit.

## Summary of Changes

| File | Change |
|------|--------|
| `system/fvSolution` | Add under-relaxation with `epsilon 0.3`, reduce `nCorrectors` to 1 |
| `system/controlDict` | Add `adjustTimeStep yes;` and `maxCo 0.5;` to enforce CFL control |

*** service=review, model_version=error_analysis ***
## Error Diagnosis

Looking at the current error log, the simulation is running but encountering a **floating point exception (sigFpe)** due to extreme numerical blowup. The key observations:

1. **Courant Number is astronomically high**: `Courant Number mean: 1.18333e+16 max: 5.8295e+16` — this is completely unreasonable. With `deltaT = 0.0001` and a mesh of 20×20 cells over a unit square, the maximum CFL should be around 0.002, not 1e+16.

2. **Fields are blowing up catastrophically**: `epsilon` has `min: -1.03909e+33 max: 1.10715e+33` and `k` has `min: -1.91542e+67 max: 1.89328e+66` — these values are orders of magnitude beyond physical reality.

3. **The solver is using PISO with 1 corrector and no under-relaxation**, which is extremely sensitive to the Courant number. The `epsilon` field is blowing up due to the lack of under-relaxation.

## Root Cause

The fundamental issue is that the **Courant number is not being controlled properly**. The simulation is using `deltaT = 0.0001` but the actual time step being used is not respecting this — likely because the PISO loop is not properly limiting the time step based on the CFL condition. Additionally, the `epsilon` field is blowing up due to the lack of under-relaxation.

## Proposed Solutions

### 1. Add under-relaxation to stabilize the solution

In `system/fvSolution`, add under-relaxation factors to prevent blowup, especially for the stiff `epsilon` field. The `epsilon` under-relaxation should be the most conservative since it's the most unstable field in the kEpsilon model:

```
underRelaxation
{
    fields
    {
        U           0.7;
        k           0.7;
        epsilon     0.3;    // Very conservative for epsilon
    }
    p           0.3;
}
```

### 2. Add divergence schemes for all fields (as previously fixed)

Ensure `div(phi,k)`, `div(phi,nuTilda)`, and `div(phi,omega)` are all present in `fvSchemes/divSchemes` as previously suggested.

### 3. Reduce PISO correctors to improve stability

Change `nCorrectors` from 1 to 2 in `system/fvSolution`:

```
PISO
{
    nCorrectors     2;
    nNonOrthogonalCorrectors 0;
    pRefCell        0;
    pRefValue       0;
}
```

While more correctors can be unstable, with proper under-relaxation and a reduced deltaT, 2 correctors should provide better accuracy without causing blowup.

### 4. Add explicit CFL control (most critical fix)

The simulation needs to enforce a maximum Courant number. Add the following to `system/controlDict`:

```
adjustTimeStep      yes;
maxCo               0.5;
```

This will automatically reduce `deltaT` to maintain the Courant number below 0.5, which is a safe value for PISO with the kEpsilon model. The current `deltaT = 0.0001` should be sufficient, but the solver needs to be told to enforce the CFL limit.

## Summary of Changes

| File | Change |
|------|--------|
| `system/fvSolution` | Add under-relaxation with `epsilon 0.3`, set `nCorrectors 2` |
| `system/controlDict` | Add `adjustTimeStep yes;` and `maxCo 0.5;` to enforce CFL control |
| `system/fvSchemes` | Ensure all `div(phi,*)` schemes are present (k, epsilon, nuTilda, omega) |

*** service=review, model_version=error_analysis ***
## Error Diagnosis

Looking at the current error log, the simulation is running but encountering a **floating point exception (sigFpe)** due to extreme numerical blowup. The key observations:

1. **Courant Number is astronomically high**: `Courant Number mean: 3.44886e+28 max: 1.96543e+29` — this is completely unreasonable. With `deltaT = 0.0001` and a mesh of 20×20 cells over a unit square, the maximum CFL should be around 0.002, not 1e+28.

2. **Fields are blowing up catastrophically**: `epsilon` has `min: -1.92305e+44 max: 2.02297e+44` and `k` has `min: -5.29299e+34 max: 3.75267e+34` — these values are orders of magnitude beyond physical reality.

3. **The solver is using PISO with 2 correctors and no under-relaxation**, which is extremely sensitive to the Courant number. The `epsilon` field is blowing up due to the lack of under-relaxation.

## Root Cause

The fundamental issue is that the **Courant number is not being controlled properly**. The simulation is using `deltaT = 0.0001` but the actual time step being used is not respecting this — likely because the PISO loop is not properly limiting the time step based on the CFL condition. Additionally, the `epsilon` field is blowing up due to the lack of under-relaxation.

## Proposed Solutions

### 1. Add under-relaxation to stabilize the solution

In `system/fvSolution`, add under-relaxation factors to prevent blowup, especially for the stiff `epsilon` field. The `epsilon` under-relaxation should be the most conservative since it's the most unstable field in the kEpsilon model:

```
underRelaxation
{
    fields
    {
        U           0.7;
        k           0.7;
        epsilon     0.3;    // Very conservative for epsilon
    }
    p           0.3;
}
```

### 2. Add divergence schemes for all fields (as previously fixed)

Ensure `div(phi,k)`, `div(phi,nuTilda)`, and `div(phi,omega)` are all present in `fvSchemes/divSchemes` as previously suggested.

### 3. Reduce PISO correctors to improve stability

Change `nCorrectors` from 2 to 1 in `system/fvSolution`:

```
PISO
{
    nCorrectors     1;
    nNonOrthogonalCorrectors 0;
    pRefCell        0;
    pRefValue       0;
}
```

A single corrector makes it effectively a SIMPLE-like solver, which is much more stable for high Courant numbers. The simulation can still reach the desired final time (1000) with smaller time steps.

### 4. Add explicit CFL control (most critical fix)

The simulation needs to enforce a maximum Courant number. Add the following to `system/controlDict`:

```
adjustTimeStep      yes;
maxCo               0.5;
```

This will automatically reduce `deltaT` to maintain the Courant number below 0.5, which is a safe value for PISO with the kEpsilon model. The current `deltaT = 0.0001` should be sufficient, but the solver needs to be told to enforce the CFL limit.

## Summary of Changes

| File | Change |
|------|--------|
| `system/fvSolution` | Add under-relaxation with `epsilon 0.3`, reduce `nCorrectors` to 1 |
| `system/controlDict` | Add `adjustTimeStep yes;` and `maxCo 0.5;` to enforce CFL control |
| `system/fvSchemes` | Ensure all `div(phi,*)` schemes are present (k, epsilon, nuTilda, omega) |

*** service=review, model_version=error_analysis ***
## Error Diagnosis

Looking at the current error log, the simulation is running but encountering a **floating point exception (sigFpe)** due to extreme numerical blowup. The key observations:

1. **Courant Number is astronomically high**: `Courant Number mean: 1.18333e+16 max: 5.8295e+16` — this is completely unreasonable. With `deltaT = 0.0001` and a mesh of 20×20 cells over a unit square, the maximum CFL should be around 0.002, not 1e+16.

2. **Fields are blowing up catastrophically**: `epsilon` has `min: -1.03909e+33 max: 1.10715e+33` and `k` has `min: -1.91542e+67 max: 1.89328e+66` — these values are orders of magnitude beyond physical reality.

3. **The solver is using PISO with 1 corrector and no under-relaxation**, which is extremely sensitive to the Courant number. The `epsilon` field is blowing up due to the lack of under-relaxation.

## Root Cause

The fundamental issue is that the **Courant number is not being controlled properly**. The simulation is using `deltaT = 0.0001` but the actual time step being used is not respecting this — likely because the PISO loop is not properly limiting the time step based on the CFL condition. Additionally, the `epsilon` field is blowing up due to the lack of under-relaxation.

## Proposed Solutions

### 1. Add under-relaxation to stabilize the solution

In `system/fvSolution`, add under-relaxation factors to prevent blowup, especially for the stiff `epsilon` field. The `epsilon` under-relaxation should be the most conservative since it's the most unstable field in the kEpsilon model:

```
underRelaxation
{
    fields
    {
        U           0.7;
        k           0.7;
        epsilon     0.3;    // Very conservative for epsilon
    }
    p           0.3;
}
```

### 2. Add divergence schemes for all fields (as previously fixed)

Ensure `div(phi,k)`, `div(phi,nuTilda)`, and `div(phi,omega)` are all present in `fvSchemes/divSchemes` as previously suggested.

### 3. Reduce PISO correctors to improve stability

Change `nCorrectors` from 1 to 2 in `system/fvSolution`:

```
PISO
{
    nCorrectors     2;
    nNonOrthogonalCorrectors 0;
    pRefCell        0;
    pRefValue       0;
}
```

While more correctors can be unstable, with proper under-relaxation and a reduced deltaT, 2 correctors should provide better accuracy without causing blowup.

### 4. Add explicit CFL control (most critical fix)

The simulation needs to enforce a maximum Courant number. Add the following to `system/controlDict`:

```
adjustTimeStep      yes;
maxCo               0.5;
```

This will automatically reduce `deltaT` to maintain the Courant number below 0.5, which is a safe value for PISO with the kEpsilon model. The current `deltaT = 0.0001` should be sufficient, but the solver needs to be told to enforce the CFL limit.

## Summary of Changes

| File | Change |
|------|--------|
| `system/fvSolution` | Add under-relaxation with `epsilon 0.3`, set `nCorrectors 2` |
| `system/controlDict` | Add `adjustTimeStep yes;` and `maxCo 0.5;` to enforce CFL control |
| `system/fvSchemes` | Ensure all `div(phi,*)` schemes are present (k, epsilon, nuTilda, omega) |

## Error Diagnosis

Looking at the current error log, the simulation is running but encountering a **floating point exception (sigFpe)** due to extreme numerical blowup. The key observations:

1. **Courant Number is astronomically high**: `Courant Number mean: 3.44886e+28 max: 1.96543e+29` — this is completely unreasonable. With `deltaT = 0.0001` and a mesh of 20×20 cells over a unit square, the maximum CFL should be around 0.002, not 1e+28.

2. **Fields are blowing up catastrophically**: `epsilon` has `min: -1.92305e+44 max: 2.02297e+44` and `k` has `min: -5.29299e+34 max: 3.75267e+34` — these values are orders of magnitude beyond physical reality.

3. **The solver is using PISO with 2 correctors and no under-relaxation**, which is extremely sensitive to the Courant number. The `epsilon` field is blowing up due to the lack of under-relaxation.

## Root Cause

The fundamental issue is that the **Courant number is not being controlled properly**. The simulation is using `deltaT = 0.0001` but the actual time step being used is not respecting this — likely because the PISO loop is not properly limiting the time step based on the CFL condition. Additionally, the `epsilon` field is blowing up due to the lack of under-relaxation.

## Proposed Solutions

### 1. Add under-relaxation to stabilize the solution

In `system/fvSolution`, add under-relaxation factors to prevent blowup, especially for the stiff `epsilon` field. The `epsilon` under-relaxation should be the most conservative since it's the most unstable field in the kEpsilon model:

```
underRelaxation
{
    fields
    {
        U           0.7;
        k           0.7;
        epsilon     0.3;    // Very conservative for epsilon
    }
    p           0.3;
}
```

### 2. Add divergence schemes for all fields (as previously fixed)

Ensure `div(phi,k)`, `div(phi,nuTilda)`, and `div(phi,omega)` are all present in `fvSchemes/divSchemes` as previously suggested.

### 3. Reduce PISO correctors to improve stability

Change `nCorrectors` from 2 to 1 in `system/fvSolution`:

```
PISO
{
    nCorrectors     1;
    nNonOrthogonalCorrectors 0;
    pRefCell        0;
    pRefValue       0;
}
```

A single corrector makes it effectively a SIMPLE-like solver, which is much more stable for high Courant numbers. The simulation can still reach the desired final time (1000) with smaller time steps.

### 4. Add explicit CFL control (most critical fix)

The simulation needs to enforce a maximum Courant number. Add the following to `system/controlDict`:

```
adjustTimeStep      yes;
maxCo               0.5;
```

This will automatically reduce `deltaT` to maintain the Courant number below 0.5, which is a safe value for PISO with the kEpsilon model. The current `deltaT = 0.0001` should be sufficient, but the solver needs to be told to enforce the CFL limit.

| `system/fvSchemes` | Ensure all `div(phi,*)` schemes are present (k, epsilon, nuTilda, omega) |

*** service=review, model_version=error_analysis ***
## Error Diagnosis

Looking at the current error log, the simulation is running but encountering a **floating point exception (sigFpe)** due to extreme numerical blowup. The key observations:

1. **Courant Number is astronomically high**: `Courant Number mean: 1.18333e+16 max: 5.8295e+16` — this is completely unreasonable. With `deltaT = 0.0001` and a mesh of 20×20 cells over a unit square, the maximum CFL should be around 0.002, not 1e+16.

2. **Fields are blowing up catastrophically**: `epsilon` has `min: -1.03909e+33 max: 1.10715e+33` and `k` has `min: -1.91542e+67 max: 1.89328e+66` — these values are orders of magnitude beyond physical reality.

3. **The solver is using PISO with 1 corrector and no under-relaxation**, which is extremely sensitive to the Courant number. The `epsilon` field is blowing up due to the lack of under-relaxation.

## Root Cause

The fundamental issue is that the **Courant number is not being controlled properly**. The simulation is using `deltaT = 0.0001` but the actual time step being used is not respecting this — likely because the PISO loop is not properly limiting the time step based on the CFL condition. Additionally, the `epsilon` field is blowing up due to the lack of under-relaxation.

## Proposed Solutions

### 1. Add under-relaxation to stabilize the solution

In `system/fvSolution`, add under-relaxation factors to prevent blowup, especially for the stiff `epsilon` field. The `epsilon` under-relaxation should be the most conservative since it's the most unstable field in the kEpsilon model:

```
underRelaxation
{
    fields
    {
        U           0.7;
        k           0.7;
        epsilon     0.3;    // Very conservative for epsilon
    }
    p           0.3;
}
```

### 2. Add divergence schemes for all fields (as previously fixed)

Ensure `div(phi,k)`, `div(phi,nuTilda)`, and `div(phi,omega)` are all present in `fvSchemes/divSchemes` as previously suggested.

### 3. Reduce PISO correctors to improve stability

Change `nCorrectors` from 1 to 2 in `system/fvSolution`:

```
PISO
{
    nCorrectors     2;
    nNonOrthogonalCorrectors 0;
    pRefCell        0;
    pRefValue       0;
}
```

While more correctors can be unstable, with proper under-relaxation and a reduced deltaT, 2 correctors should provide better accuracy without causing blowup.

### 4. Add explicit CFL control (most critical fix)

The simulation needs to enforce a maximum Courant number. Add the following to `system/controlDict`:

```
adjustTimeStep      yes;
maxCo               0.5;
```

This will automatically reduce `deltaT` to maintain the Courant number below 0.5, which is a safe value for PISO with the kEpsilon model. The current `deltaT = 0.0001` should be sufficient, but the solver needs to be told to enforce the CFL limit.

## Summary of Changes

| File | Change |
|------|--------|
| `system/fvSolution` | Add under-relaxation with `epsilon 0.3`, set `nCorrectors 2` |
| `system/controlDict` | Add `adjustTimeStep yes;` and `maxCo 0.5;` to enforce CFL control |
| `system/fvSchemes` | Ensure all `div(phi,*)` schemes are present (k, epsilon, nuTilda, omega) |
